===== PAGE 276 =====
Guess Who Came For A Visit?
Abraham pours some drink for Brad Fletcher and Lowell Figur.
vnnsEs
Thousands of years ago, Moses or Moshe Rabbeny
(Moses our teacher) found his way to Mount Sinai. The
Commandments he brought down still provide the same
impact upon Hues today.
On Sunday, March 4, 1979 at 10:00 a.m., Moses once
again brought the message of the Ten Commandments to
the descendents of these same Israelites. He appeared on
the roof of the Hecht-Gordon-Bossen School Wing of the
Jewish Center to hand down the same message he
brought from Sinai ages ago.
How joyous it was to hear and see Moses, and a great
celebration took place at that time. Children of our Sunday
School participated in this momentous occasion as did
their parents. Moses also made an appearance for the
Day School and Afternoon School students.
Our forefather Abraham visited the
Jacksonville Jewish Center. In his tent
he told the children how he destroyed
the idols his father sent him to feed, and
how he entertained the angels in his tent.
Abraham (Rabbi Dov Kentof) said he is
planning a return visit, as nomads move
around and do return to good places. Our
students are looking forward to rejoining
him to learn more about his life and times.

Here comes the Bride
Lunch-time
CAMP STAFF - Top row; Rob Weinberg, Assistant
Program Director, Daniella Wind, Shelly Kulchin,
Program Director, Blanche Slott, Administrative
Director, Joanne Davis, Steve Goldman, Missy
Levine, Morry Lasris. Bottom row; Holly Ettlinger,
Arthur Miller, Robin Jerard and Julie Spitzer.
The Center Day Camp is an
integral part of the Center youth
program giving children between the
ages of three and fourteen the oppor
tunity to experience new skills and creative
activities in a warm, friendly Jewish atmos-
phere. We pride ourselves that we continue to
serve the Jewish community with the only Jewish Day
Camp in the Jacksonville and Orange Park areas.
Starting in mid-June the Camp season continues for eight
weeks. Much consideration is given in the selection of an out
standing staff of specialists, Counselors, Junior Counselors and
Counselors-in-T raining.
The four two-week sessions for campers age five through four-
teen years include a special sports camp featuring basketball,
baseball, soccer and a variety of other sports. Arts and crafts,
always a popular activity, supplies materials to inspire the creative
ability of campers of all ages. Older campers experience the joy of
creating clay pottery, batik and weaving. Each session includes
overnight camping and field trips.
We welcome campers of three and four years of age for eight
weekly half-day sessions. This program includes crafts, play-
ground, story telling, movies, snacks and lunch.
All groups have instructional swimming instruction taught by
qualified Water Safety instructors. Water sports also include free
swim periods, races and competitive swimming and canoe instruc-
tion. The camp fee compares with that of other day camps and
includes insurance, snack and lunch. Further information is avail-
able in the Center Office or at the camp office during the summer
sessions.

209
kadima canventinn
The Jacksonville
Jewish Center Kadima
hosted a convention of
approximately 200 teen-
agers (6th, 7th, and 8th
graders) on February 2,
1979. Youth from Miami,
Clearwater, Sarasota,
Tampa, St. Petersburg,
Gainesville, Orlando,
Lakeland, Atlanta, Geor-
gia, Charlotte, North
Carolina participated.
The theme of the con-
vention was “All Begin-
nings Are Difficult”, The
Bar/Bat Mitzvah Years.
Through various me-
diums such as socio-
drama, parent/teen
panel discussions, inti-
mate study groups, the
many aspects of this
period in a young per-
sons life were explored.
The convention made
excellent use of all our
facilities. Many of the
Kadimaniks described
the convention as “the
best yet!”
The Chalutzim Aw Cemingf
5th and 6th Graders ONLY!!!
Call the Youth Department - 268-6736
Co-advisors: Rhoda Goldstein and Scott Zimmerman

TO OUR ADVERTISERS:
Our constant gratitude, not only for making the publication
possible, but also for the support they lend to our Youth
Activities. We urge our members to reciprocate with their
patronage.
• A reference and guide for the Jacksonville Jewish Center
membership and the Jewish community.
• Serves over 7,000 members and advertisers.
• All proceeds devoted to the Center’s program.
• The only Jewish publication in the community listing all
groups.
The Year Book is a summary of the various activities and
program of this Synagogue-Center depicted in pictures and
words. We are grateful to the many organizations of this
community who have cooperated in providing us with
material used.
We appreciate the efforts of our staff and other members of
the Center who have devoted time and effort on behalf of our
1979-80 Center Yearbook.
FLORENCE ROBIN
Secretary
JACK DORMAN
Co-Chairman
IRVING GHELERTER

159
Our Jewish ótors
Don Morris, photographer, receives a plaque from Rabbi
Dov Kentof. For once Don was on the other side of the
camera.
A
TRIBUTE
The new logo around Jacksonville is
“Capture The Spirit”. Not only does it apply
to our city, but it certainly describes Don
Morris’ photography.
As the official photographer of the Jackson-
ville Jewish Center, Don Morris has given
generously of his time and equipment to
“Capture The Spirit of the Jacksonville Jewish
Center” and all its activities.
It has truly been an educational and delight-
ful experience working with Don. No matter
when I have asked him to come to the Center
he has been there. His cheerful disposition
and good humor have made the job of editor a
very pleasant one. Cheers to 100 more years!
—Isabel Balotin,
Editor

SIMHAT TORAH CELEBRATION — TUESDAY. OCTOBER 24. 1978
CONGREGATION TO HONOR THREE LEADERS FOR OUTSTANDING SERVICE
The Festival of Sukkot reaches its joyous climax
on Simhat Torah, the last day of the Holiday. Simhat
Torah is the happiest holiday on the Jewish calendar
because we celebrate our joy and pleasure with the
Torah.
Because of Israel’s perennial love of the Torah,
it has been referred to in Jewish tradition as Israel’s
“bride.” A tradition evolved in ancient times to honor
the individual called for the last reading of the Torah
—the Hatan Torah or the groom of the Torah. The
person honored to begin the Torah reading from its
beginning is called Hatan Bereshit the groom of
Genesis. We also honor a woman who has made a dis-
tinctive contribution to our Synagogue and to Jewish
life in general—the “Woman of Valor” honor. We
will honor these individuals at Services on Simhat
Torah morning, Tuesday, October 24.
Services on Simhat Torah Tuesday, October 24
begin at 9:00 a.m. and will include the Hakafot Torah
Scroll Procession. A reception honoring Burton I.
Grossman, Edwin Presser and Ms. Minnie Schreiber
will be held immedately following Services.
The entire congregation extends heartfelt con-
gratulations to Burton and Bea Grossman, Edwin and
Anne Presser and Minnie Schreiber and their families
on this very special moment in their lives.
******
BURTON I. (Bud) GROSSMAN
This year Burton (Bud) Gross-
man will receive the honor of the
Hatan Torah (Bridegroom of the
Torah). Bud has been an active
member of the Finance, Education
and Membership Committees. He
continues to serve on the Building
Fund Committee with the same
dedication he showed when he serv-
ed as our Synagogue President and
Chairman of the Board.
Under Bud’s capable leadership
the School Building at Third and
Silver Streets was constructed with-
out an increase in our mortgage.
Philip Selber, who served as
Chairman of the Board during
Bud’s Presidency, described him as
“a most effective leader because he
himself set an example for the con-
gregation, with his high ideals and
sense of values.”
Even now, in matters of great im-
portance, when senior thought and
advice is needed, Bud is always
consulted. He is greatly respected
by all people with whom he works.
He is a most honorable man, a rie-
voted husband to his wife Bea,
a loving grandfather, and a proud
father of two daughters who have
both displayed leadership qualities
like their father. His daughter,
Ellen Freedman is the immediate
past president of our Sisterhood.
Gail Rice, his other daughter, was
recently elected President of the
Sisterhood of Tefereth Israel in
San Diego, California.
EDWIN PRESSER
Selected to receive the honor of
Hatan Bereshit (Bridegroom of the
Beginning) is Edwin Presser. A
member of the Board of Directors
for twenty years, Ed served as
Vice-President for ten of those
years. He was Chairman of the
Finance Committee and served as
a member of the Building Fund
Committee.
As our main legal counsel, Ed
has represented us on may historic
occasions. He advised us during the
acquisition of our present property
on State Road 13 and assisted in
securing the loan for the said pro-
perty. He was also intensely invol-
ved with the sale of the Third and
Silver Street building.
His willingness to give of his own
time and legal expertise has been
a great personal sacrifice. With
a deep sense of loyalty he has serv-
ed the Center unselfishly. The en-
tire membership is grateful for his
untiring support.
We honor Ed for his time and
commitment for the Jacksonville
Jewish Center. His wife, Anne, and
his children, Marilyn, Stephen and
Jeffrey, all share in this Simha.
MINNIE SCHREIBER
Minnie Schreiber, Chairperson of
the Library Committee, has been
chosen to be our Woman of Valor.
For over fifteen years Minnie has
devoted endless hours of planning
so that our Library will serve as a
complete media resource Center for
the schools and the entire congre-
gation.
River Garden has been another
project Minnie is completely dedi-
cated to. She was the first woman
President and is presently Chair-
person of the Board. Her disting-
uished activities have earned her
recognition in “Who’s Who in
American Women.”
Governor Askew has chosen Min-
nie to be a delegate to the Gover-
nor’s Conference of Library and
Information Services in Tallahas-
see. The knowledge Minnie has
gained from her activties, she brings
to the Center. Minnie is now chair-
ing a sub-committee that is devel-
oping plans for the Rita Gendzier
Exhibit of Judaism.
A devoted Jewess, active not only
in the Jewish community, but all
phases of civic activities. The Cen-
ter takes a great deal of pride in
her work.
===== PAGE 324 =====
23
"We weren’t only buying for the future, we were buying for now.”
Louis Safer
The key analysis is that even if we never built a
Jewish Center on this piece of property in a million
years, we had a great summer camp", Spevak said.
"We already had a large house on the property
and we would be paying just over $1,000 an acre
for a permanent camp site. If we lived for an eter-
nity with that proposition we couldn’t lose. If we
ever decided to build our synagogue there, it would
be great. Everything came our way in time.”
Others involved in the selection process agreed
that the camp provided the needed incentive to
purchase the property.
"The thing that compelled us to go forward was
the campsite.” Margol said, "That was the driving
force and Sam (Spevak) couldn’t have found a
better piece of property. The main reason we could
sell the idea of purchasing the property was that
Bob Fischer was tearing his hair out every year
over where to go for a campsite”, recalls Lou Safer.
"We weren’t only buying for the future, we were
buying for now”.
After much debate, sometimes heated, the
Center Board voted to go ahead with the purchase
of the land.
A contract was signed on May 24, 1963, said
Safer, who was acting as the Center’s attorney.
The sellers of the property were listed as Agnes
Lechlider (who resided in the house) and Maybelle
F. Abernathy.
The Olympic A. A. U. Pool during construction as seen in April
1964. One of the first Olympic size pools built in the Jackson-
ville area, the pool is now used by the Day Camp, congregation,
and as a recreational facility available to the community at large
for rental.
In order to obtain the $20,000 needed to close
on the deal, 10 persons were rounded up. Each of
them endorsed a $2,000 note from the Central
Bank. The ten included Louis Portnoy, M. W.
Hollins, Eli Edwards, Wilbur Margol, Louis Safer,
Herman Weiss, Philip Selber, Jack Rosner, Ben
Friedman and B. B. Yoffee.
On August 9, 1963, the closing was held. Ten
months later, a mezzuza was affixed to the door
of the house on the Center’s new property. The
rest is history.
Affixing the mezuzah, with Sam Price Chairman of the Con-
struction Committee placing the final nail in the door of the
existing house at the future home of the Center. Looking on
left to right: Philip Selber, Center President; Jim Clements,
representing the architectural firm of Freedman and Clements;
Louis Safer, Chairman of the Building Fund; and Rabbi
Turetsky.
First services conducted at the new site in conjunction with
the preliminary dedicatory services and Open House on Sunday,
May 31. Officiating, Rabbi A. Turetsky and Cantor A. Marton.
